() , ? asked the Minister of Petroleum and Petroleum Resources Development,:

(a) Will he inform this House (i) the total profit of the Ceylon Petroleum Corporation for the years 2006 and 2007; (ii) how the total cost of sales per liter is composed of; and

[.. 11.55] . ( . ) (The Hon. R. Sampanthan) Thank you, Mr. Deputy Chairman. Today, we are having the Committee Stage Discussion on the Presidents Vote. As you all know, the Government has today enunciated that it is pursuing four concepts in order to find a solution to this countrys national question. They are: demilitarization, democratization, development and devolution. This is, as defined by the President. When I spoke during the Second Reading Debate of the Budget, I dealt with the concept of demilitarization, somewhat exhaustively, and in the course of my speech today, I first propose to deal with this so-called concept of "democratization". The Tamil people, Sir, have since 1956, through their democratic verdicts overwhelmingly supported the right to internal self-determination in the areas of their historical habitation. Initially, even several Muslim leaders were elected from the Eastern Province on the Federal Party ticket. If the demand of the Federal Party for a federal arrangement was accommodated, many more members of the Muslim community would have been

returned on the Federal Party ticket. I would submit that President Mahinda Rajapaksa should acquaint himself with this history before imagining that democracy is being introduced into the North-East by him with the assistance of certain paramilitary groups in 2007 - 2008. This position of President Mahinda Rajapaksa, I submit, is ludicrous. President Mahinda Rajapaksa should realize that not merely did you not accommodate the legitimate aspirations of the Tamil people in keeping with their democratic verdicts, you subjected them to several racial pograms over several decades when there was no violence whatever on the Tamil side. That was your answer to our legitimate aspirations and our democratic verdicts, to the nonviolent Satyagraha campaigns that we engaged in. Today not merely President Mahinda Rajapaksa, but some of his sidekicks have the temerity to try to teach the Tamil people about democracy. Several decades later after the armed struggle commenced, some areas in the North-East went out of Government control and when elections were held you did not want to locate polling booths for those areas, in such areas. You did not want the electoral process to take place in areas not under your control. You clustered such polling booths and located them in Government controlled territory, some considerable distance away from the residence of the voters. It is true that the LTTE discouraged voters living in areas under their control from going and voting in clustered booths located in areas under Government control. The losers were Tamil candidates, such as myself and several others like me; nobody else - certainly not any one of you. Nevertheless, the Tamils who were returned at those elections were returned on the basis of the same policy - the right to internal self-determination in the areas of their historical habitation. This is an indisputable fact and I challenge President Mahinda Rajapaksa to prove the contrary. Instead of engaging in senseless rhetoric, I would appeal that you kindly get your facts straight. At the 2001 Parliamentary Elections, when the peace process had virtually commenced - the Norwegian facilitators were functioning in the country - the Tamil people in large numbers in the uncleared areas attempted to come through the Army checkpoints and vote at the clustered booths in the Government-controlled territory. They were prevented by the Armed Forces from crossing the checkpoints and voting. President Mahinda Rajapksa was a Member of the Government that was responsible for that action. Several of these persons filed fundamental rights applications in the Supreme Court and I believe about five or six of them, from both the North and the East, were awarded damages by Justice Mark Fernando, then a senior judge of the Supreme Court. Who subverted democracy by preventing these Tamil people from voting? Was it not the Government of which you were a Member? And you have the impudence to talk about restoring democracy to the Tamil people. At the 2004 Parliamentary Elections these Tamil people in the LTTE-controlled areas who were

2008 17 117 118

able to cross the checkpoints voted liberally. There may have been some irregularities -these people were voting for the first time after several decades but there was, however, not the slightest doubt about whom the people wanted to elect. Twenty out of twenty one Tamil Members elected from the North and the East were from the Illankai Tamil Arasu Kadchi. The Illankai Tamil Arasu Kadchi also obtained two seats on the National List on the strength of the vote they polled in the North-East. The 22 of us in Parliament are unquestionably the representatives of the Tamil people of the North-East, which unfortunately, your Government does not want to acknowledge in view of the agenda that you have. Having conducted a disgraceful and shameful election in the Eastern Province, you have the temerity to talk about the election of the Illankai Tamil Arasu Kadchi Members in 2004. We know what happened at the Eastern Provincial Council Election. On my recent visit to Trincomalee, I met with some people from the North of my district where several booths had been clustered during the Provincial Council Elections; many of the voters had left the villages, they had gone away to other parts of the country or had left the country. At 5 oclock in the morning on election day, I was told, a bus and 25 other vehicles arrived in that particular village where the booths of several villages had been clustered and about 150 people alighted from these vehicles; they went into several houses in that village, used their toilets and their water facilities to freshen themselves and set about stuffing the ballot boxes. A roly-poly Minister in charge of relief in your Government and a six-foot Government party organizer of one the Colombo District electorates were prominent people among these miscreants. Still, you could not win a single seat; not one Tamil Member from your party was elected in Trincomalee. That was the way you got about conducting elections; that was the way you conducted the Eastern Provincial Council Election. In fact, there have been c e r t a i n a c t i o n s f i l e d i n c o u r t a n d , I believe, when those hearings take place more facts in regard to the manner in which you conducted the Eastern Provincial Council Election will come to light and will be proved in the court; how young fellows, members of a paramilitary group with whom you are in alliance, were moving around with weapons and having their own way. All these matters will come to light. And you have the impudence to say that you conducted a proper election. I challenge you to prove that at the Parliamentary Elections in 2004, in any part of the North-East, any such disgraceful and shameful incidents as I have described a few moments ago occurred. Completely abusing government authority and using to the hilt a paramilitary group, you narrowly won an election in the Eastern Province when the most important Tamil political party - the Illankai Tamil Arasu Kadchi - was not in the fray. Do not delude yourselves that after all the atrocities committed by you on the Tamil people they, by conviction, will be with you. You think that you can

subjugate them with military force and buy them with some peanuts while you proceed with your agenda of furthering Sinhala nationalism, particularly in the Eastern Province. The Tamil speaking-people are not going to be satisfied with your peanuts - Kachchankoddai. You may be satisfied, but we are not. They want the power, the authority to be able to manage their own affairs in the areas of their historical habitation where they have lived for centuries, in keeping with their dignity and self-respect. I challenge you to hold an internationally conducted and monitored referendum to enable the Tamil-speaking people in the North-East to decide what they want and to tell the people, tell the world, what they want. Hold an internationally-sponsored referendum and ask the Tamil-speaking people in the North and the East what they want, accept their verdict, and give them what they want. That would be the most honourable way towards ascertaining the wishes of the Tamil-speaking people in the North-East, rather than resorting to the various subterfuges that you are presently engaged in. Before I deal with, Sir, development and devolution, the other two concepts of this Government towards the resolution of this national question, I should place on record the Governments multi-faceted position on the people who inhabit this country, their status in this country, their rights in this country and other relevant issues. I will start off by referring to what the President had said in recent times. He has given an interview to Mr. N. Ram, the Chief Editor of The Hindu newspaper, a gentleman whom we know very well, which appeared on the 29th of October, 2008. One of the questions posed by Mr. Ram is: You have repeatedly said your government is committed to a political solution of the Tamil question in Sri Lanka. What will be the contours of this political solution? President Mahinda Rajapaksa in his answer states, I will quote from the relevant paragraph:

Let me reiterate that my government is firmly committed to a negotiated political solution - based on devolution of power and ensuring the democratic, political, including linguistic, rights of all our Tamil brethren within an undivided Sri Lanka. I would like to see more devolution to the people. It must go to the grassroots level, because they must decide on their development work, what they need. We must allow them to participate in the whole process." I have nothing against the Hon. Susantha Punchinilame who is here. His father was my contemporary in the 1977 Parliament. You are busy in the Eastern Province. But people do not want you to be busy in the Eastern Province. People want to elect their leaders in the Eastern Province to be busy and look after their matters. The next question that was asked from the President by Mr. Ram is:

How do you view the concerns expressed in India and elsewhere over the adverse impact of the military operations on a large number of Tamil civilians in the Wanni?

[ . ]

119 120

The answer the President gave was: We are making, and will continue to make, every effort to avoid civilian casualties. We will do everything in our power to mitigate and resolve the plight of the civilians displaced or affected by the conflict. We will rehabilitate every civilian affected by the conflict in a fair and transparent way. When I last spoke in Parliament during the Second Reading of the Budget, I placed on record details of several events that have occurred in the Wanni after the Special Envoy, the Hon. Basil Rajapaksa went to New Delhi and gave an assurance to the Central Government in New Delhi that Tamil civilians will not be harmed. I also placed on record pictures of several events to prove that people had been killed, non-combatant civilians had been killed, had been injured, houses had been destroyed or damaged, temples had been damaged, and even the Kilinochchi Hospital had been damaged. Despite the assurance of the President, all these things have happened. I placed on record in this House, in the course of an Adjournment Debate in September, 2007, the names of 261 Tamil persons who were killed in the Eastern Province during the course of your military activities in the Eastern Province. Have you paid compensation to any one person? I called upon your Government to appoint a Commission of Inquiry comprising three retired members of the higher judiciary, a Sinhalese, a Tamil and a Muslim with the Muslim as the Chairman, to go into that question and ascertain the truth. Have you done that? You see, you say one thing but you never act accordingly. This has been your history. The other question asked from him is: What is your reading of the position taken by the Tamil Nadu Chief Minister and Government on the current situation in Sri Lanka? The answer of President Rajapaksa is: I have respect for Tamil Nadu Chief Minister M. Karunanidhi - one of Indias senior-most politicians - and appreciate his thoughts and proposals for a just political solution of the current conflict within the framework of an undivided Sri Lanka. I would place before the House the last question asked by Mr. N. Ram from the President: Mr. President, what is your vision of an ethnically harmonious Sri Lanka? The answer is: I am absolutely clear that Sri Lanka belongs to all its citizens - Sinhalese, Tamils, Muslims, others. The policy of my Government is to uphold the equality, liberty, fraternity, and development of people belonging to all ethnic, linguistic, and religious communities.

This is what the President says. Now, whether he believes in that, whether he will formulate his policies in keeping with that, and how he will take things forward,

I do not know. But that is what he has said. But we have certain things that have happened in the past, on the basis of which we can make our own judgements. Now General Sarath Fonseka has also given an interview to the Daily Mirror on the 26th of September, 2008. He was very frank about what he has to say. He says, I quote :

I strongly believe that this country belongs to the Sinhalese That is very different to what President Rajapaksa says. He goes on saying, I quote :

..but there are minority communities and we treat them like our people, In other words, there are also these fellows, these Tamil fellows, these Muslim fellows. This country belongs to the Sinhalese people. But there are the other minority communities, the Tamil fellows, the Muslim fellows and we treat them like our people. If we do not want to treat them like our people we will treat them differently. "We being the majority of the country, 75 per cent, will never give in"; no accommodation, no compromise; we will never give in "and we have the right to protect the country. This country is not only his. This country is also mine. I have an equal right to protect this country as much as him. I do not have a Portuguese name. I have a Tamil name. What he said further, I quote : We are also a strong nation. He says that it is a Sinhalese nation; it is a strong nation. He goes on saying, I quote : They can live in this country with us. We are ..a strong nation That is the Sinhalese nation, the strong nation. He goes on saying, I quote :

They can live in this country with us. But they must not try to, under the pretext of being a minority, demand undue things. We must not ask for our protection. We must not ask for a fair share of resources in this country; we must not ask for power to deal with our affairs in the territories in which we are a majority and in which we have historically been a majority; ask for no rights; live with us at our mercy and take what we give you. That is Sarath Fonsekas position. He is the Commander of the Sri Lankan Army on whom this Government is largely dependent for conducting the present war and on whom even the political future of this Government depends. The political future of this Government is entirely dependent upon the way General Sarath Fonseka would eventually conduct this war to a finality.

2008 17 121 122

Now after that of course, there was Ven. Sobitha Thero, General Secretary of the Jathika Hela Urumaya who picked on what General Sarath Fonseka said. His statement appears in the Daily Mirror of 2nd of October, 2008. Ven. Sobitha Thero said, I quote : Ven. Sobitha Thero said that Sri Lanka is the country of Sinhala people who built its history and civilization. So, that is what Ven. Sobitha Thero, the General Secretary of JHU says. I have read to you what the President says. Having read what Venerable Sobitha Thero said, I would like to read to you what has been said by the chief ideologue of the Government today and I think, the person who formulates the ideological policy of the Government, particularly in regard to the minorities. I would like to state what the Hon. Champika Ranawaka, Minister in the Government said in an interview, published in the Daily Mirror on August 11, 2008. It states, I quote : It is the old paradigms that believed in the political solutions. But the President says, I quote:

Let me reiterate that my government is firmly committed to a negotiated political solution ... But Champika Ranawaka says, I quote : It is the old paradigms....- [Interruption.] I did not disturb you. Please do not disturb me - [Interruption.] Please behave yourself -[Interruption.] I have not been a militant. He further says, I quote: This vocabulary even exists only within the NGO, INGO and embassy officials of western nations. Why we negate these claims of an ethnic problem needing political solution is because of the peaceful manner all three communities always lived in this country till LTTEs terrorism started. According to this person, there were no anti-Tamil pogroms in 1950s; 1956, 1958; in the 1960s. Even I was locked up in Panagoda in 1961 for performing Satyagraha with my leaders in front of the Kachcheri and preventing the Government Agent from entering his office. There were no racial pogroms in the 1970s. Everything started only after the LTTE came into being. This is nothing but downright muck! Downright muck and he is an ideologue of the Government. I will leave him there, Sir. Then he gave a further interview which was even more illuminating. That was the interview that he gave to "Daily Mirror" of 16th October, 2008. It states, I quote: The Tamils have no homeland in Sri Lanka, its only in India.

Tamils have no homeland in Sri Lanka. It is only in India; in Tamil Nadu. Do you want them to go to Tamil Nadu or Tamil Nadu to come here? That is the question that you have to decide. Going on further he says, Sir, I quote: This time around it is Gen. Sarath Fonseka who decides the path the war will take. He is very clear about it. The war is being conducted not by the President Mahinda Rajapaksa; the civilian Commander-in-Chief of the armed forces. He very categorically says, This time around it is General Sarath Fonseka who decides the path the war will take. And he goes on to say, I quote: The Defence Secretary as a former military man and the General has every right to speak of majority rights. Here, he defends General Sarath Fonsekas statement in regard to the Sinhalese people. There is a another very important thing that he says. The Hon. Champika Ranawaka, your ideologue who defines your ideology in regard to the minority peoples who are living in this country, the Tamils and the Muslims - there is no question about it . He is one of the closest advisers of the President. We know that . It states, I quote: The Sinhalese are the only organic race of Sri Lanka. Other communities are all visitors to the country, whose arrival was never challenged out of the compassion of Buddhists. But they must not take this compassion for granted. The Muslims are here because our kings let them trade here and the Tamils because they were allowed to take refuge when the Moguls were invading them in India. What is happening today is pure ingratitude on the part of these visitors. Sir Paul Peiris in his historical work says that long before the advent of Vijaya who was the precursor of the Sinhala race, there were in Sri Lanka, several Eshwarams of Lord Shiva, Koneshwaram in Trincomalee facing the great Bay of Koddiyar, Thirukeshwaram in Mannar, Munneshwaram in Chilaw, Naguleshwaram in Jaffna and Thondeshwaram somewhere in down South. That is our history. Before Vijaya came here, there were Eswarams of Lord Shiva in several parts of this country, but he says that Muslims came here to do trade and we came here because the Moguls chased us out. The other thing he says, which is the most important thing and the crux of the matter is, I quote again from the "Daily Mirror" of 16th November: The only difference is that once the LTTE is destroyed no solution can be forced upon us by anyone. In other words, your intransigence, your obduracy, your obstinacy not to find a political solution which is what everybody is demanding; India is demanding; the International Community is demanding. So, you are militarily going after the LTTE not because they are a terrorist organization, not because you want to annihilate them for that reason, but because you feel that they are a force who can compel you to arrive at a political solution

12 - PL 003465 - (2008/12)

2008 17 123 124

acceptable to the Tamil-speaking people. Your ideologue has let the cat out of the bag and has admitted that the reason for the LTTE to be destroyed is that when the LTTE is destroyed, there will be no force that can compel the Sri Lankan Government to arrive at a political solution. The Sri Lankan Government does not believe in a political solution. So, this is the truth and the President keeps on saying various things and of course this wise man has also in the rush said, I quote again: I personally feel that we dont need the GSP anyway. He does not want the GSP Plus. So, you see, Sir, this is the position. I have read to you the statements of these people. We know of the "Mahinda Chintana". We know of the two pacts the President signed with the JVP and the JHU before the presidential election. The "Mahinda Chintana" and the pacts signed with the JVP and the JHU are only for a unitary state and no ISGA, no P-TOMS arrangement, nothing whatever. They are all at complete variance with the position that the President has taken in an interview to the "Hindu" where he talks of a political solution and the equality, liberty, fraternity and all that type of thing. The positions taken up by him when he contested the presidential election are a complete variance with the concepts he has defined. Of course his main military man, and I would say his main political man have enunciated their positions. The Hon. Dinesh Gunawardena can come here and sit and shout, but the Hon. Patali Champika Ranawaka is much more important than him in the corridors of power. We know that. I saw today the Gunawardena brothers standing up very vociferously for the Rajapaska brothers in Parliament. I could not but laugh at this spectacle. That is another matter. How seriously, Sir, can one take the utterances of the Government when your policy clearly indicates that what you want to do is to circumvent the minority peoples, circumscribe the minority peoples, emasculate them and exclude them from all power sharing arrangements, in a meaningful way. You are merely trying to assuage the international community who are constantly whether it be India, the USA, the Co-chairs, the European Union or any other country, wanting you to come to a political solution, emphasizing the need for political proposals that can lead to a solution. In fact, I quoted when I spoke in Parliament last during the Second Reading of the Budget, the Hon. Mangala Samaraweeras press interview where he said that the President had assured the Prime Minister of India that the final political proposals will be made public before the end of August 2006, two years ago. Of course, the President cannot defy the international community. He has got to keep on saying something. I saw the Prime Minister speaking on TV last evening. He was also striking a slightly different note. In my submission, he is playing for time to perform a gigantic deception. You are hoping that with the aid of these paramilitary groups, the TMVP in the Eastern Province and the EPDP in the Northern Province, you can show the

world that the Tamil people whom you are bombing from the air, your multi-barrel rocket launchers are killing or being injured, whose houses are being destroyed, whose temples are being destroyed, whose hospitals and schools are being destroyed, plantation crops, animal husbandry, fishing equipment and farming equipment they are all being destroyed, they are being rendered destitute, impoverished and in a state of penury, that they have come to your side, that by political conviction, they have embraced the Mahinda Chintana with the TMVP in the Eastern Province and the EPDP in the Northern Province. You are hoping that you can perpetrate this gigantic deception on the whole world and then you can say that we are doing development, we do not need devolution, and everything is in our hands. We urge the Government to rethink this whole question. We as the political party - I heard you shouting out and saying - you told the UNP and the JVP. I knew this problem would arise and that is probably one of the reasons why I called for a Division, to make sure that who was where and what the Governments reaction to that would be. We are not koti . I am not a kotiya. You talk of a fraudulent 2004 Election. You summon the Government Agent in Trincomalee, the Elections Officer in Trincomalee, the DIG, Trincomalee, and the SSP, Trincomalee, any public official in Trincomalee and ask them how that election was conducted and how did Mr. Sampanthan conduct the election? They would say we cannot point out a little error, a little wrong committed by Mr. Sampanthan. That is the answer they will give you. We are not kotiyas and we will never become kotiyas. But, please do not think that by calling us "kotiya" you can ride roughshod over our people. We will not allow you to do that. ( ) (The Hon. Dinesh Gunawardena) You are with the kotiya. . ( . ) (The Hon. R. Sampanthan) We are committed to that. I am not with the kotiya. You are a [ .] [ ] [Expunged on the order of the Chair.] kotiya yourself. ( ) (The Hon. Dinesh Gunawardena) You said that you are with the LTTE. Just five minutes ago, you said that you are with the LTTE and that you stand with the LTTE - [Interruption.]

125 126

. ( . ) (The Hon. R. Sampanthan) Please finish and sit down then I will answer you - [Interruption.] Yes, of course- [Interruption.] Please finish and let me answer you. There was a ceasefire agreement; there were international facilitators. Talks were taking place between the Government of Sri Lanka and the LTTE. You were a member of the Chandrika Bandaranaike Kumaratunga Government. You were clinging on to her sari pota when she was talking to the LTTE. Can you deny that? You are talking big now. You were clinging on to Chandrikas sari pota, like you are now clinging on to Mahinda Rajapaksas shawl. You are now clinging on to Mahinda Rajapaksas shawl. You all talk- [Interruption.] ( ) (The Hon. Dinesh Gunawardena) Hon. Member, during elections, you tried to negotiate with Chandrika Kumaratunga - [Interruption]. . ( . ) (The Hon. R. Sampanthan)

Of course, yes - [Interruption.] ( ) (The Hon. Dinesh Gunawardena) You were giving false promises to Chandrika Kumaratunga - [Interruption]. . ( . ) (The Hon. R. Sampanthan)

Please sit down. [interruption.] Of course, I negotiated with Chandrika Bandaranaike Kumaratunga. There is no question about it. I did not hide that. The whole world knew about it. The whole world knew that I was very seriously involved. The Prime Minister knew. You were not there. You do not know but the Prime Minister was there, when I went to Temple Trees and met with the President. I negotiated. So, Sir, we are interested in the cause of our people. We are interested in this problem being resolved in a manner where our people will be secure, they will be safe, they will have a future in this country, the Tamil-speaking people. We still want that. But, if you cannot give us the right to internal self-determination in our areas of historical habitation, then, international law says that we shall be entitled to the right of external self-determination. Please remember that ! Please remember that and do not think that you can shout down reason, you can shout down justice, that you can suppress us. That will be a mistake. I thank you, Sir.

) (The Hon. Muthu Sivalingam - Deputy Minister of Estate Infrastructure) , , . . , , , , , , . 1997 ' ' , . . "" , , . , , . 13 , . - . . , , . '' . '' . , . , . , .

2008 17

. . , , 6.00 5.00 . ? , . . . . . , . - 250 250 . , ; , . , . , .

Estate Infrastructure Development . In 2006, the UNDP provided technical assistance to the Ministry of Estate Infrastructure to prepare a National Action Plan for social development of the plantation community. The reduction of poverty that is increasing in the plantation sector will be a challenge to the achievement of the Millennium Development Goals in Sri Lanka, targeted by the year 2015. Therefore, the UNDP was concerned with the reduction of poverty in the plantation sector before the targeted year. The National Action Plan was prepared with the participation of the professionals, intellectuals, Government officers, representatives of trade unions, NGOs and other minor stakeholders in the plantation sector. An international consultant and three national consultants, commissioned by the UNDP, worked more than five months to prepare this plan. The Cabinet of Ministers had approved this plan in 2002. The National Action Plan has identified the investment need for projects such as health, education, employment, housing and water supply, rehabilitation of estate roads, supply of electricity, post and telecommunication, gender equality, human rights and community development, which are targeted to reduce poverty in the plantation

sector and the need to complete the projects within a period of 10 years. We need about Rs. 900,449 million to implement these projects. It is not an easy task for a Government to allocate money through the Budget to fulfil this requirement within a short period. Therefore, this year His Excellency the President has allocated Rs. 25 million in order to formulate a programme and start these projects next year for which we will be able to seek assistance from foreign agencies and finish it within ten years. , . , .

, , , JEDB, SPC . . , . , 10 . . , 10 - 15 , , , . . ; . , . , . ; . , ; . . . , . I thank the Secretary to the Ministry of Estate Infrastructure as well as my Additional Secretary and my staff for all the co-operation

179 180

[ ] extended to me in ensuring the smooth running of the work in the Ministry. I also want to thank especially the Hon. Arumugam Thondaman, our General Secretary who is always ready to help and guide me. . . , . , . , . [.. 3.39] ( ) (The Hon. (Dr.) Jayalath Jayawardana) , . , . , , . . . ; . , . . , . . . , . , , , .

ADJOURNMENT ( ) (The Hon. Nimal Siripala de Silva) , " " . . . Question proposed. ( ) (The Deputy Speaker) . . () . ( ) (The Hon. Nimal Siripala de Silva) " () " . , . . Question put, and agreed to. , () .

, , (.) . Whereupon MR. DEPUTY SPEAKER left the Chair, and THE HON. (VEN.) UDAWATTE NANDA THERO took the Chair. ( ) (The Presiding Member) .

FINANCIAL STRENGTHENING OF SRILANKAN AIRLINES ( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake)

Thank you, Ven. Presiding Member, for giving me this opportunity to move an Adjournment Motion which is important to the aviation industry from a commercial perspective. I move, "SriLankan Airlines is the national carrier of Sri Lanka. Mihin Air Limited was formed in November, 2006. It operated for a couple of months and has run aground utilizing 3,200 million SLR of public finance. Furthermore SriLankan Airlines was also handed over to Government of Sri Lanka owing to the fact that Emirates Airlines walked out of the agreement with Sri Lankan Airlines. This is now loosing money and has total a loss of US $ 120 million from the day the Government of Sri Lanka received the management. We would like to know as to why tax payers money cannot be used for a better use if not use the allocation of 6,000 million SLR to SriLankan Airlines and strengthen it financially. " As you know, Ven. Presiding Member, on the 1st of April, 2008, SriLankan Airlines was handed back to the Sri Lankan Government. Prior to that, you had aviation handled by Air Ceylon, Air Lanka and the SriLankan Airlines respectively with the subsequent privatization with Emirates. Then, we had the dawning of Mihin Air. The Adjournment Motion that I have put forward today is regarding SriLankan Airlines which has been handed back to the Government. While you have SriLankan Airlines, you also have Mihin Air which runs parallel to it; lost a sum of Rs.3,200 million and further infusion of capital is going to take place. The rationale behind in doing so is only known to a few at the expense of many, and we would like to know at this particular moment as to what the purpose is in doing so. SriLankan Airlines was handed over to the Sri Lankan Government in the month of April - I may be subject to correction in the variation. The overall loss up to end of October has roughly been in the range of about US Dollars 130 million. The loss in the month of April was US Dollars nine million; in May it was US Dollars 20 million; in June it was US Dollars 24 million; in July it was US Dollars 18 million; in August it was US Dollars 27 million; in September it was US Dollars 14 million, and I am informed that in October, it was about US Dollars 11 million. This total sum up to about US Dollars 130 million and in Sri Lankan Rupee terms, is roughly about Rs.13 billion or Rs.13,000 million. This, I would say at the outset is the worst type of a scenario that an

225 226

16 - PL 003465 - (2008/12)

2008 17

airline can bring into existence. The reason has nothing to do with Sri Lanka, but owing to the international meltdown that has taken place and with the simmering that is taking place in the Middle Eastern region with the unsettled climate that is there, it has had a downward trend in world tourism. So, with that, you have SriLankan Airlines which is coming on to us, as well as Mihin Air that is being promoted at the expense of Sri Lanka and the Sri Lankan public at large. You would see that in 2006, there was a haphazard approach with the BOI in trying to bring into existence a new company called, Mihin Air. Within a couple of days you had got the aviation approval and got started. At that particular moment, Ven. Presiding Member, we, in this House, mentioned that - with the knowledge of aviation that we possess - it is not the conducive climate to start a secondary airline. It was known that this budget airline that was coming in to compete with the other airlines was also going to compete with SriLankan Airlines that was going to be handed back to us, owing to the fact that the Emirates Agreement was up for renegotiation. But, at that particular moment, there was an earnest appeal saying that there is a necessity to have cheaper tickets be provided to the migrant workers as well as to certain elderly people who want to go for worship, and on that they started the airline. The foundation was not correctly put in place at the starting off of that particular airline. So, before too long, what we basically said would happen, had happened. You had the passenger loads in the range of about 30 to 40 per cent. You had three - four flights, which were relatively old and as a result the maintenance was relatively high and the full usage of flying was not possible. Before too long, you saw the financial tremors taking place. It had an exposure of almost Rs. 3,200 million and this has been quite aptly mentioned by none other than the Minister of Power, the Hon. Mahindananda Aluthgamage. He said that a colossal sum of Rs. 3,200 million has been lost and further, called upon the Government that if there has been mismanagement to take necessary action against those responsible. Certainly, while defending the decision to start Mihin Air, he was taking to task the people who have run the airline and run it aground. So, this is not something that comes from the Opposition just for the sake of saying something but in the national interest, we have been saying this from day dot. I did mention this even when AirLanka was to be privatized that it was not the way it has got to be done - certainly there were some people who opposed it - and finally, that Minister went to courts, apologized and a couple of months back he came before this House and said, "Yes, the decision was wrong." Likewise, when you wanted to start Mihin Air, we said, "Do not do it. There are better options to be looked at". Unfortunately, it was done and you have spent Rs. 3,200 million and finally it has run aground. Now, Rs. 3,200

million has been infused into an entity without assets in hand. That is the biggest problem that we have. You have today in the international arena the financial meltdown which is severe. Today, America, the European Union countries, Japan, the second biggest trading country, their financial markets are in chaos; recession has set into these countries. With this situation prevailing, we are investing even more heavily into SriLankan Airlines and Mihin Air and the reason of our debating today is to see that these two are amalgamated. I must say, with all that there was a breath of fresh air when the Hon. Chamal Rajapaksa took over. He, at least had the courage to tell the people who were mismanaging to get the hell out of the place. When I met him subsequently, I congratulated him on that and that type of praise merits attention whether it comes from the Opposition or anybody. But, that did not stop the public finances going in Though you took corrective action and told the people who were messing up to get the hell out of the place, what could not be stopped was the continuous operation that was taking place even without him. That is the problem. Now today, you have Rs. 1, 200 million outstanding from Mihin Air to Bank of Ceylon; interest frozen. Now the Bank of Ceylon says, "Interest back, it is about Rs. 300 million." Mr. Asantha de Mel, Chairman of the Ceylon Petroleum Corporation coming public says, "Our problem with Mihin Air is, their debts are outstanding. That is the reason why we have got to increase petroleum prices". So you have almost Rs. 650 to 700 million outstanding and when you add all those together, it is about Rs. 2.1 billion. Then, further, with the expenditure on salaries and accommodation for officers et cetera, Rs. 3,200 million has run aground. Now, with that in the background, you have allocated another Rs. 6,000 million for Mihin Air under Head 113, Programme 2, Project 3, sub Project 14. Hon. Minister, you are taking this money to re-beef up Mihin Air when SriLankan Airlines is struggling to survive; they have no assets, they have only Rs. 14 billion in cash. You have Mr. Manoj Gunawardena as the CEO of SriLankan Airlines and I must say that product knowledge is there in him. But you have given him a grenade, removed the pin and told him to run the place which is impossible for anybody; even if the Chairman of the British Airways comes in, it is impossible. So this is why we are saying you need not put money into an airline that has already made losses. Why do you not put that money into SriLankan Airlines if you want to do so? Furthermore, the reason why you want to run Mihin Air is that you want to send people to Buddhagaya or to the Middle-East. Well and good! Your intention may be pure. But why did you spend Rs. 3, 200 million? If you divide it by the number of passengers flown, you could have given them a Rs. 15,000 rebate and told them to fly SriLankan Airlines. That is the problem. Venerable Presiding Member, we will be passing another

227 228

[ ]

Rs. 6,000 million in this House through this Budget for Mihin Air whereas in the Decentralized Budget, an Hon. Member gets Rs. 5 million and for all 225 MPs it is only Rs. 1.1 billion. Is that fair? It is six times more. I mean, we do 10,000 times more work than they do. Then, look at the increase in the monthly allowance given to the soldiers engaged in action. In the operational areas you have roughly - [Interruption.] ( ) (The Presiding Member) , . ( ) (The Hon. (Dr.) Mervyn Silva) , . , . ( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) That has no relevance to this. That is not a point of Order. ( ) (The Hon. (Dr.) Mervyn Silva) ; . . , ,-[ ]

( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) So, on the basis of increasing the monthly allowance from Rs. 3,000 to Rs. 5,000 for the soldiers engaged in action, the allocation made there is Rs. 4.5 billion. So, Mihin Air has Rs. 6 billion and for the soldiers you have only Rs. 4.5 billion. Is that fair? Then, look at the proposed milk subsidy to be given to the children of this country. There is a general feeling that every child in this country gets a glass of milk.-[Interruption.] ( ) (The Presiding Member) , . ( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) But when we were going through the Committee Stage Discussions, we found to our horror that only 34,000 children in this country get a glass of milk. We thought that almost 1.5 million children get a glass of milk

everyday. So, this is a travesty of justice; you allocate only Rs. 900 million to give milk to 34,000 children and Rs. 6,000 million on Mihin Air. So, what is the rationale - [Interruption.] I do not need to waste my time on guys who do not know what the debit and credit is or who do not know what Mihin Air and SriLankan Airlines are. This guy just goes on like a jack-in-the-box and keeps on shouting. It does not make any difference whether he shouts or not. So, on the basis of Rs. 6000 million being allocated for Mihin Air development and only Rs. 900 million being allocated for milk subsidy, we want to know what the purpose is in doing this? I am sure the Hon. Minister has some sense in trying to do this because I see him in a different context to the rest. So, going on that basis, Hon. Minister, why are you wasting money on re-fleeting and retargeting a different company when you can strengthen SriLankan Airlines? Now, look at the situation of SriLankan Airlines. Basically, routes like Colombo-London are important but you have reduced the flights from 14 to 7 because of the cost factor. Then, you have drastically reduced the flights to India. - [Interruption.] There is no difference, whether he shouts or not, I will go on. So, that has brought an impact on the revenue of the company. Then, with regard to Colombo-Singapore, I was informed today that there was a cancellation of a flight due to lack of passengers. Even the existing airline does not run properly for the simple reason that there are no passengers. Now if you look at Colombo-London, the economy class ticket of SriLankan Airlines is roughly Rs.110,000, but you can fly Kuwait Airways, RJA and the rest of them for Rs. 67,000. So, on that basis you have a point : the highest cost factor. So, if you are trying to resurrect an airline, you have got to act according to the fundamentals that are there; you have to be competitive, you have to keep your costs down, you have to ensure that you compete with the rest of the airlines. So on that particular score I ask, what is going on? You have the fuel prices coming down. That benefit has not been given to the passengers. Other airlines are much more responsive. You have the little that comes on rupee. There is no loyalty factor for SriLankan Airlines. More Sri Lankans today are flying on non-Sri Lankan airlines for the simple reason of rupees and cents. Hon. Minister, you are basically trying to say that you want to give the benefit to the Sri Lankans. But, if you divide Rs. 3,200 million by the passengers flown, you will find that you could have given a Rs. 15,000 rebate to a passenger and he could have flown SriLankan Airlines. Because, when flying to Maldives, it is not cheaper than SriLankan Airlines; when flying to Dubai, it is not cheaper than SriLankan Airlines or Air Arabia. I mean, you have got to look at it in the context of competition. If you say, the fare on Sri Lankan Airlines is x and the rest are flying at the same fare as of SriLankan Airlines, that is a different matter. But you have got Air Arabia which roughly costs Rs.12,000 - 13,000 and in no way can Mihin Air compete with that. You have Mihin Air competing with Singapore Airlines.

229 230

2008 17

It has no chance in competing with other cheap airlines. With that, you have got to strengthen SriLankan Airlines. You cannot run Sri Lankan Airlines and Mihin Air and be competitive in both areas. If you have the necessity, ensure that you strengthen SriLankan Airlines. I was on a flight the previous week in India. The pilots are very concerned. They are not paid international prices. You have got to have a 10 per cent increase in flying. You know the passenger rights in the Indian market. Today Kingfisher is in trouble, Indian Airlines in trouble, Jet Air is just scraping their barrel, Malaysian Airlines is retrenching. So, if the other international airlines have a 5 per cent growth, more pilots will be taken into those airlines and then what will happen is, SriLankan Airlines would not be able to retain the pilots who are there. ( ) (The Presiding Member) , . ( ) . . , ? ( ) (The Presiding Member) 13 . ( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) . . 12 , . ( ) (The Presiding Member) , 13 . ( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) Now SriLankan Airlines is trying to reduce certain flights and fly to Rome. Just because of the numbers, it does not mean that there is any profit. So, all we want to say is, ensure that you make SriLankan Airlines more competitive, ensure that you have a higher load factor in that and have a more cargo load. Now, I see certain Deputy Ministers giving answers stating that you have got to export vegetables, fruits and plants by Mihin Air. Mihin Air aircraft cannot carry 600 kilograms. Even if you fly the entire year, you would not be able get more than Rs. 10 million. So, you must have product knowledge when you talk on this. Even when we spoke on Air Lanka, we spoke with a sense of feeling for the company; feeling for the country. Now, again I am

saying, do not waste this money, ensure that you put it into better use. The opportunity cost is so great that you will never be able to make Mihin Air another Sri Lankan airline. On that score, all I want to say is, do not politicize this industry. Ensure that you look at it with a proper judgemental factor when you transfer that money into SriLankan Airlines. Otherwise, SriLankan Airlines will also run down financially and you would neither have SriLankan Airlines nor Mihin Air. The sky can be yours. , . . . ( ) (The Presiding Member) . , . ( ) (The Hon.
